<text>I left my wallet behind in the car as I was dropped off at the airport. I tried waving down the taxi driver before he drove off, but he was already gone. Panic ensued. I began calling the taxi line.  Multiple dispatch people did not want to help, and I was told to call x number,  call y number, oh go online and fill this form, disregarding I had a flight to catch. They said they would send the gentleman back out to me at no-charge, that he had my wallet, and that he was just finishing up another ride. This took about an hour and a half, and five phone calls.

The gentleman arrived, whom which I did enjoy great conversation which on my ride up there. I think the service to the airport was not a problem, and obviously me leaving my wallet in the car is not his fault. I offered him $20 as a thank you for bringing back my wallet, he explained that I would need to pay for a full car ride. As I did not know where he was coming from, I felt this was unfair, especially after being told it was a good samaritan act, and tipping him 20% on the cab fare earlier.  He demanded $40 from me, stating he was at dinner with family, which I believe to be a lie as dispatch said he was on another drive, and it only had been about an hour and a half in the middle of rush hour. I offered him $30, and he became irate. With me needing to run to my flight, I took the high road, gave him the $40, and went on with my day.

I believe this experience could be improved on these issues:

1. Drivers should check if the customer may have left something behind prior to departure, or if they're waving at them to at least stop, the above scenario could be avoided. This is a nice touch that could really save someone, and really up the customer service game.

2. Being told the driver would come meet me out of good will, is one thing. If it is goodwill, please communicate that to the driver, or at least communicate what the fee is ahead of time, as I have no idea or any way to actually validate where the driver came from, or have the ticker running to show the length of the drive. < text>
Awful.  I called Yellow Cab to request a cab to take me to the San Francisco airport.  The dispatcher asked for my name and address, and then asked if I need the cab now or was reserving it for later.  I told him I needed it now and asked how long it would take.  He responded "15 minutes."  Ten minutes later I was standing on the street corner waiting.  Half an hour goes by.  Nothing.  I called Yellow Cab to request an update on my cab.  My previous dealings with their phone system have taught me that if you have a pending ride, the automated system will say so in order to avoid multiple calls.  However, when I called the automated system did no such thing and instead I was transferred to a dispatcher.  The dispatcher was not only extremely rude but utterly unhelpful.  First I asked for a status update about my cab and the dispatcher was unwilling to give me an update.  Finally after bickering back and forth for several minutes, the dispatcher finally said "let me see if the driver is still on his way."  Excuse me?  I ordered the cab, no cab picked me up, so why would the driver not be on his way?  After being on hold for several minutes I was displeased to learn that the driver had "bailed" (the dispatcher's word, not mine).  Meaning, the driver had decided to cancel my ride without warning.  When I asked the dispatcher why the driver would not have the decency to inform the call center the dispatcher responded by saying that the calls were controlled via a computer system and that the cab driver did not have to call to inform the call center that he was cancelling my ride.  This would be fine except for the fact that no one at the call center attempted to send a new cab, or contact me to see if I still needed a ride (which, guess what, I did).  When I pointed that out to the dispatcher, the response was "we don't do call outs."  I politely requested another cab, told the dispatcher to rush it, and that I would not be canceling the ride.  My cab showed up a few minutes later and I talked to the driver about it, who stated that the dispatch system did indeed get notice of a cancelled fare but that the dispatchers had a habit of doing nothing.  While the drivers for Yellow Cab seem friendly enough the actual "Customer Service" people and all of the dispatchers are disgustingly lazy and incompetent.  Don't waste your time or money.</text>

< UserId.>
107152190076731796260</UserId.>
<name>Peter Xaymountry</name>< Date>
1611631546599< /Date>
<rating>5<//rating>< Review>
Such a great choice when taking advantage of their 3 for 10 dollars special. Since my company moved to Simi Valley, I started trying places here since we don't have a fridge in the office yet. I had a reward to use for their 3 for 10 dollars special going so I was able to get my sirloin steak. For my sides I just got double fries and chips/salsa for my appetizers. I was bummed they didn't have the Texas fries as an option. Ordering online and selecting curbside pickup was so easy. When it was my time to go pick up my order, I was the only one there probably cause I put in my order right when they open. This Chili's location is shared with Costco so be prepare for the traffic inside the lot while going in and exiting. When I pulled up to the designated pickup spot, I sent a text that I was there and someone came out within 5 minutes to give me my order. The lady was very friendly and made sure I had all my sauces in the bag. I love their Sirloin Steak, keep in mind when you get your food that's hot .. open the container a little bit so the steam escape and doesn't continue to cook your food. My office is across the street so I didn't have to do that for my food.< /Review>

I have noticed it getting markedly more popular though.  The last time I was there, the place was packed and there were people waiting, so I recommend making an appointment, just to be safe. When you do, your tech meets you at the door and you are VIP'd straight to a waiting chair.  There is a huge difference in price between the regular pedicure, and the spa pedicure, so be sure to ask for prices along the way, when you are offered something.  I do the spa pedi because my skin feels so wonderful afterward. I love the exfoliating massage part of it, but it does climb up to $35 by the time you add the nail art. I think their pedi prices are reversed on their spa package list, so I can't advise you on which description to use - the euro, deluxe or regular. But you'll want to confirm the price and details of each. The music and atmosphere are very relaxing.  Hard to believe with so many people in the same room, but it's easy to fall asleep in the massage chairs.< /text>
